<div class="hcfe-content">     <section class="primary-container"> <div class="page-width-container">   <article class="page"> <section class="article-container" st-ve="35"><h1>Download your data</h1><div class="cc"><p>You can export and download your data from the Google products you use, like your email, calendar, and photos. In a few easy steps, create an archive to keep for your records or use the data in another service.&nbsp;</p>

<p><strong>Note</strong>: Downloading your data does not delete it from Googles servers. Learn<a href="/accounts/answer/32046"> how to delete your account</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a href="/websearch/answer/465">how to delete your searches and browsing activity</a>.</p>

<h2>Create an archive of your data</h2>

<h3>First, choose which products to include</h3>

<ol>
  <li>Visit the <a href="https://www.google.com/settings/takeout" target="_blank">Download your data</a> page. You might have to sign in to your Google Account.</li>
  <li>Choose which Google products to include in your download. To see more details and options for a product, select the Down arrow <img src="//lh3.googleusercontent.com/dW0yyTPf131NnuLju8o-VuiHWYkxcb6MLAfu8hKNjYOoA3euoyQEGc9YiruwUjhzJ9U8=w18-h18" width="18" height="18" alt="Down Arrow" title="Down Arrow">.</li>
  <li>Select <strong>Next</strong>.</li>
  <li>Choose your archive's "File type."</li>
</ol>

<p><strong>Note:</strong> Your content from Google Play Music isn't included when you create an archive. Learn how to <a href="/googleplay/answer/1250232">download your music</a>.</p>

<h3>Next, choose how your archive is delivered</h3>

<p>When your archive is created by using one of these options, we'll email you a link to its location. Depending on the amount of information in your account, this process could take a few minutes or several hours. Most people get the link to their archive the same day that they request it.</p>

<div class="zippy-wrapper"><a class="zippy" name="email">Send download link via email</a>

  <div>
    <p>We'll email you a link to download your archive.</p>

    <ol>
      <li>For "Delivery method," select <strong>Send download link via email</strong>.</li>
      <li>Choose <strong>Create archive</strong>.</li>
      <li>In the email that arrives, click <strong>Download archive</strong>.</li>
      <li>To download your data, follow the onscreen instructions.</li>
    </ol>
  </div>
</div>

<div class="zippy-wrapper"><a class="zippy" name="drive">Add to Drive</a>

  <div>
    <p>We'll add your archive to <a href="https://drive.google.com/" target="_blank">Google Drive</a> and email you a link to its location. Your data will count toward <a href="https://www.google.com/settings/storage" target="_blank">your storage</a>.</p>

    <ol>
      <li>For "Delivery method," select <strong>Add to Drive</strong>.</li>
      <li>Choose <strong>Create archive</strong>.</li>
      <li>In the email that arrives, click <strong>View in Drive</strong>. You'll see a folder with your data organized by product.</li>
      <li>To download your data, at the top of the screen, select Download <img src="//lh3.googleusercontent.com/z2G5n0pmvU4jGmb2tQosFbFfL8yGI0enZPfhT7-AwhqoXWqJ7xSbWFOove8V4pc3qXU=w18" width="18" height="18" alt="Download" title="Download">.</li>
    </ol>
  </div>
</div>

<div class="zippy-wrapper"><a class="zippy" name="dropbox">Add to Dropbox</a>

  <div>
    <p>We'll upload your archive to <a href="https://www.dropbox.com/" target="_blank">Dropbox</a> and email you a link to its location.</p>

    <ol>
      <li>For "Delivery method," select <strong>Add to Dropbox</strong>.</li>
      <li>Choose <strong>Link account and create archive</strong>.</li>
      <li>You'll be directed to Dropbox. Sign in to your Dropbox account if prompted.</li>
      <li>In the Dropbox window that asks if Google Download Your Data can access its own "Apps" folder in your Dropbox, select <strong>Allow</strong>.</li>
      <li>To keep your data private, make sure you're not sharing this Dropbox folder with anyone else.</li>
      <li>In the email that arrives, click <strong>View in Dropbox</strong>. You'll be taken to the Dropbox folder with your archive.</li>
      <li>To download your data, follow Dropbox's process to download files.</li>
    </ol>

    <p><strong>Notes</strong></p>

    <ul>
      <li>After you follow these steps, Google Download Your Data will show up in your Dropbox security settings as a linked app. You can remove Google as a linked app at any time. (If you export data to Dropbox in the future, you'll need to give Google access again.)</li>
      <li>When your archive reaches Dropbox, Google is no longer responsible for it. Your archive will be covered by the <a href="https://www.dropbox.com/terms" target="_blank">Dropbox Terms of Service</a>.</li>
    </ul>
  </div>
</div>

<div class="zippy-wrapper"><a class="zippy" name="onedrive">Add to Microsoft OneDrive</a>

  <div>
    <p>We'll upload your archive to <a href="https://onedrive.live.com" target="_blank">Microsoft OneDrive</a> and email you a link to its location.</p>

    <ol>
      <li>For "Delivery method," select <strong>Add to OneDrive</strong>.</li>
      <li>Choose <strong>Link account and create archive</strong>.</li>
      <li>You'll be directed to Microsoft. Sign in to your Microsoft account if prompted.</li>
      <li>In the Microsoft window that asks if Google Download Your Data can access your info, select <strong>Yes</strong>.</li>
      <li>To keep your data private, make sure you're not sharing this OneDrive folder with anyone else.</li>
      <li>In the email that arrives, click <strong>View in OneDrive</strong>. You'll be taken to the OneDrive folder with your archive.</li>
      <li>To download your data, follow OneDrive's process to download files.</li>
    </ol>

    <p><strong>Notes</strong></p>

    <ul>
      <li>After you follow these steps, Google Download Your Data will show up in your Microsoft OneDrive security and privacy settings as an app that can access some of your info. You can remove Google's access at any time. (If you export data to OneDrive in the future, you'll need to give Google access again.)</li>
      <li>When your archive reaches Microsoft OneDrive, Google is no longer responsible for it. Your archive will be covered by the <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/servicesagreement/" target="_blank">Microsoft Services Agreement</a>.</li>
    </ul>
  </div>
</div>

<h2>Common questions</h2>

<div class="zippy-wrapper"><a class="zippy" name="format">Which format should I choose for my data?</a>

  <div>
    <p>Deciding what format you should choose depends on the service, type of data, and your intended use of it. We have chosen types that we believe are the most useful and portable.&nbsp;For example, we export contacts as vCard, which is a very common format for email providers. We often will also provide additional options to fit your specific needs.</p>
  </div>
</div>

<div class="zippy-wrapper"><a class="zippy" name="store_data">Where should I store my data?</a>

  <div>
    <p>You can store your data anywhere that is safe and has enough room for it. In most cases, it is easiest to download it directly to your computer.</p>

    <p>If you use a public computer, store it in Google Drive or an alternate storage space where you are the only user.</p>

    <p><strong>Note:</strong> If you use Google Drive&nbsp;and plan to delete your Google Account, you'll have to move your archive to a different storage space before deleting your account.</p>
  </div>
</div>

<div class="zippy-wrapper"><a class="zippy" name="mult_files">Why was my archive broken into multiple zip files?</a>

  <div>
    <p>In order to make sure your data will be downloaded, we limit these zip files to 2GB. Archives that are larger than 2GB are split into multiple zip files. Selecting the tgz or tbz format for your archive will increase the size limit to 50GB, so it is much less likely that your archive will be split.</p>

    <p><strong>Note:</strong> Special software may be required to unpack a tgz or tbz archive. Keep in mind that these types of files can't have unicode characters in the file names.</p>
  </div>
</div>

<div class="zippy-wrapper"><a class="zippy" name="expire">Why do my archives expire?</a>

  <div>
    <p>Your archive expires in about 7 days. After that time, you'll want to create a new archive with your most up-to-date information.</p>

    <p>An expired archive doesn't mean your data has expired, and you won't experience any change in Google services as a result.</p>

    <p><strong>Note:</strong> We only allow each archive to be downloaded 5 times; after that, please request another archive.</p>
  </div>
</div>

<div class="zippy-wrapper"><a class="zippy" name="pw">Why do I have to enter my password again when I try to download my archive?</a>

  <div>
    <p>The security of your data is very important, so when you create an archive, we want to make sure that you're the only person downloading your data.</p>

    <p>To do that, we ask you to re-enter your Google Account password if you haven't recently. We understand that this may be inconvenient, but it's important to take extra steps to keep your data safe.</p>

    <p><strong>Note</strong>: If your account has 2-Step Verification turned on, you may also be asked for an additional verification code that will be sent to your phone.</p>
  </div>
</div>

<div class="zippy-wrapper"><a class="zippy" name="not_work">Why didn't my archive work?</a>

  <div>
    <p>If something goes wrong with your archive or you're not able to make one, try creating another one. This approach often fixes the problem.</p>
  </div>
</div>

<div class="zippy-wrapper"><a class="zippy" name="Gmail_labels">How do I preserve my Gmail labels if I am exporting my mail?</a>

  <div>
    <p>When you export your mail from Gmail, each message's labels are preserved in a special X-Gmail-Labels header in your download file. While no mail client recognizes this header now, most mail clients allow for extensions to be written that could make use of the labels.</p>
  </div>
</div>

<div class="zippy-wrapper"><a class="zippy" name="org_data">I'm a G Suite customer. How do I export my organization's data?</a>

  <div>
    <p>See <a href="/a/answer/100458">Migrate data away from G Suite</a>&nbsp;for options on how to migrate your organization's email, calendars, documents, and sites.</p>
  </div>
</div>

<h2>Send us feedback</h2>

<p><a href="/accounts/contact/takeout_feedback">Let us know about your experience</a> downloading your data. By sharing your feedback, you help Google improve this product for you and other people.</p>
